        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer251706506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16670085594993909173">I love it when people write reviews that are EX.AC.TLY. on par with how I felt about a book. This <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42066599' rel='nofollow noopener'>one</a> in particular gets it spot on. <br/><br/>I was really disappointed by Inkdeath. Not gonna lie. I finished it several days ago and have sat around trying to think of positive things to say about it but I got nothin'. This is by far the weakest book in the trilogy and should have been much shorter and much less lame. Dangit. <br/><br/>This book is not quite a total departure from Inkheart and Inkspell but it's pretty</span>
  <span id="freeText16670085594993909173" style="display:none">I love it when people write reviews that are EX.AC.TLY. on par with how I felt about a book. This <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42066599" rel="nofollow noopener">one</a> in particular gets it spot on. <br /><br />I was really disappointed by Inkdeath. Not gonna lie. I finished it several days ago and have sat around trying to think of positive things to say about it but I got nothin'. This is by far the weakest book in the trilogy and should have been much shorter and much less lame. Dangit. <br /><br />This book is not quite a total departure from Inkheart and Inkspell but it's pretty close. None of the characters feel fleshed out in Inkdeath. Farid in particular - he never gets over his weird obsession with Dustfinger. Now, having weird obsessions with father figures of my own, I feel pretty confident in saying that Farid needs to seek some serious mental help. That whole part of the story just didn't ring true to me, honestly. I get being concerned for Dustfinger, but not obsessed to the point of stalkerishness with him. Creepy. <br /><br />Meggie finds a new, completely random and weird, love interest. It actually ties into the story decently with Fenoglio remembering that he'd written a short story about that particular character but it was never published. But it's still random and weird. And the love interest character never feels like a part of the integral cast.<br /><br />Mo's character was probably the least disappointing here. He went through a pretty awesomely harrowing torture sequence with Orpheus near the end. But even then, the ending felt odd and kind of disjointed. And totally not what I expected. <br /><br />So, I'm glad I read Inkdeath because yay closure! But at the same time, I think I would have preferred a different ending like the one that was good in my head. I also would have liked to know the baby's name, just because I'm curious like that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16670085594993909173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10642955463826487807" style="display:none">(spoilers)<br /><br />I learned that the first book of this trilogy is unfortunately the best book in this trilogy. <br /><br />While the ending is good there are major flaws in the text:<br />1. And the moral of the story is that life always seems better in books than rather the one we live on a daily basis... but sometimes you go to the world and realize its extremely violent and that Brendan Fraiser is your dad and you wonder what the heck you got yourself into in the first place.</span>

<div id="review_31656893" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31656893" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1464083-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219776622p2/1464083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31656893?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1464083-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780439866286" href="/book/show/2986863-inkdeath">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the series</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer31656893&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31656893" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer251414902381500826">Warning: MAJOR spoilers. <br/><br/>I'm really disappionted.<br/><br/>First of all, it took way too long to get into this book. During the first 200-300 pages, I was like "What?" I didn't really care about the characters, and nothing they did piqued my interest. It was bland. Maybe bad editing, or maybe bad writing, I couldn't really tell. But I think someone could have safetly cut a LOT of pages from the manuscript without losing that much. I mean, the first books weren't small, but I felt like a lot happened. But </span>
  <span id="freeText251414902381500826" style="display:none">Warning: MAJOR spoilers. <br /><br />I'm really disappionted.<br /><br />First of all, it took way too long to get into this book. During the first 200-300 pages, I was like "What?" I didn't really care about the characters, and nothing they did piqued my interest. It was bland. Maybe bad editing, or maybe bad writing, I couldn't really tell. But I think someone could have safetly cut a LOT of pages from the manuscript without losing that much. I mean, the first books weren't small, but I felt like a lot happened. But this one . . . it was like pulling teeth. I had to force myself to keep reading, with the vain hope it would end better and redeem itself.<br /><br />Needless to say, it didn't.<br /><br />And then some stuff started to happen, but I still didn't care.<br /><br />I was reduced to skimming the last hundred or so pages, because I just couldn't take it anymore. It's a shame, since I absolutely loved the first two books, and was looking forward to this one, and the upcoming movie. <br /><br />And the end. God, what <i>was</i> that? Meggie falls in love with this random guy (was he in the first two books? I can't remember, but I don't think so.) JUST because Fenoglio wrote something like that? So Meggie is now at the mercy of the writing? When did <i>that</i> happen? Poor Farid. Meggie just completely leaves him in the dust. I felt so bad for him, and I wanted to shake some sense into Meggie. She came across as a whinny child throughout the whole novel, and it came to the point where I really didn't want her to talk.<br /><br />And they stay in the Inkworld? Why? <br /><br />WHY?<br /><br />And the baby in the beginning, and the little cameo he gets at the end? What was the point of that? <br /><br />Oh, and don't get me started with Mo. He bugged the crap out of me. Really, Mo? Risk your life and stay in la-la land just because you <i>want</i> to?<br /><br />Resa bothered me too, but I couldn't pin point why. I just found her annoying and irritating.<br /><br />I'm just sad. This series had so much potential, and the first two were so good.<br /><br />Ugh. I'm so disappointed with the end of this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="251414902381500826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3098762791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer459955850166004725">I just can't get over it how perfectly written this series is!<br/>I came here after having read aloud "His Dark Materials" to my boys and there were so many moments in this highly recommended to me series that had me facepalming and even my boys shouting out what an idiotic turn of event or decision this-and-that was.<br/><br/>Not a single time did this happen to us in the Inkheart trilogy. Quite on the contrary. The buildup of the characters and the world is top notch, each event is a logical conclusion with</span>
  <span id="freeText459955850166004725" style="display:none">I just can't get over it how perfectly written this series is!<br />I came here after having read aloud "His Dark Materials" to my boys and there were so many moments in this highly recommended to me series that had me facepalming and even my boys shouting out what an idiotic turn of event or decision this-and-that was.<br /><br />Not a single time did this happen to us in the Inkheart trilogy. Quite on the contrary. The buildup of the characters and the world is top notch, each event is a logical conclusion within the plot itself. Most of the characters are deeply layered, flawed and feel absolutely real.<br /><br />The tone in this third volume of the series changed towards a much darker mood as well in terms of character introspective as in terms of plot. My boys (10 and 12 years) weren't as fond of it as of the enchanting first book, yet my initial resentments quickly dissolved. It is definitely better suited for a more mature audience. A deep melancholia weaves through everything in this book that requires a bit more life experience. I was wondering why Cornelia Funke changed her prose - until I read that her husband was dying of cancer while she was writing and then everything made sense and added even more depth to what I was reading.<br /><br />I am in awe of an author who is able to deliver such high quality throughout a trilogy with roughly 2800 pages.<br /><br />This is a book for booklovers about booklovers whose lives are inexorably changed by written words. A brilliant entanglement where the author never once looses sight of a single thread.<br /><br />Cornelia Funke is one hell of an author and has my undiminished admiration. I'm so happy that I decided to read this trilogy to my boys and I'm looking forward to the fourth volume.</span>
  <a data-text-id="459955850166004725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17924864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17924864" />
    <a title="MountainLaurel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/998422-mountainlaurel"><img alt="MountainLaurel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216649696p2/998422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17924864?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MountainLaurel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MountainLaurel" href="/user/show/998422-mountainlaurel">MountainLaurel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer17924864&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17924864" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13157502258763609775">I'd been anticipating this book for a long, long time, so my expectations were high. Also it had been a while since I'd re-read <i>Inkheart</i> or <i>Inkspell</i>, so some things were hard for me to remember.<br/><br/>The writing was as beautiful as the first two books, and several chapters (especially #8) were very moving and eloquent. In that, it didn't disappoint me at all. My main complaint is that Dustfinger almost completely lost his charm. Before, he had been pretty much one of my favorite literary characters EV</span>
  <span id="freeText13157502258763609775" style="display:none">I'd been anticipating this book for a long, long time, so my expectations were high. Also it had been a while since I'd re-read <i>Inkheart</i> or <i>Inkspell</i>, so some things were hard for me to remember.<br /><br />The writing was as beautiful as the first two books, and several chapters (especially #8) were very moving and eloquent. In that, it didn't disappoint me at all. My main complaint is that Dustfinger almost completely lost his charm. Before, he had been pretty much one of my favorite literary characters EVER, and even though I was glad he was risen from the dead I didn't like how he "became Mo's shadow" or whatever; it completely took away from his enigmatic-ness and his general character, really.<br /><br />Farid was basically shoved to the side in this book, which I didn't mind since I'd never liked him much anyway (yes, I know I'm the only one!), but it seemed a little abrupt how Doria just ran in and Meggie fell for him and that was that.<br /><br />The middle of the book was really good and I was quite enthralled, but towards the end it seemed like Cornelia was rushing the story. The Adderhead died so quickly and then Mo and Resa and Dustfinger and Brianna all went back to the giant tree, which took about one page. Since it's the end of the series I had hoped for more.<br /><br />I liked how everyone stayed in the Inkworld...I'd sort of been expecting them to feel like they had to go home when it was all over, so that was nicely different.<br /><br />All together, <i>Inkdeath</i> was very good but it didn't quite measure up to the other two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13157502258763609775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=2015-challenge">2015-challenge</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1427622347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3672370176405462623">I read Inkdeath as a buddy read with a friend. This one wraps up the Inkheart trilogy. I am so glad I started and got to finish this trilogy. I must say that I would not class this as a middle grade series. It is very complex and also has some content that I would not think suitable for younger readers.<br/><br/>I really rather liked this book from the trilogy more than the first two. From the start of the series I always liked the plot of being able to read yourself into or out of a story. This one went </span>
  <span id="freeText3672370176405462623" style="display:none">I read Inkdeath as a buddy read with a friend. This one wraps up the Inkheart trilogy. I am so glad I started and got to finish this trilogy. I must say that I would not class this as a middle grade series. It is very complex and also has some content that I would not think suitable for younger readers.<br /><br />I really rather liked this book from the trilogy more than the first two. From the start of the series I always liked the plot of being able to read yourself into or out of a story. This one went much deeper than the first two in to the world they were read into. Even though this one felt like it had so much more depth it was still easier to follow and it was also very engaging.<br /><br />Once again I loved the characters and how well they developed over the three books. I did not find that I enjoyed Mo as much in this one for reasons that I will not include here. Readers should be able to experience all of that themselves. I think this series is a great one for some unexpected surprises.<br /><br />I recommend this to anyone who loves fantasy, or maybe some mystery and thriller all rolled into one. Just remember that this is pretty complex story and some content may not be suitable for younger readers. in my opinion. This last book is a great wrap up of the story and totally worth reading all of them.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ho2UHPfICc2NQxI5z38ALClqJy399D9eUd4zqrFXorskq/3OTJbApSpoplg4igrz/zXA5TN5sTkKoHUbfBRQIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16249908764254481732">Cornelia Funke is a multiple award-winning German illustrator and storyteller, who writes fantasy for all ages of readers. Amongst her best known books is the Inkheart trilogy. Many of Cornelia's titles are published all over the world and translated into more than 30 languages. She has two children, two birds and a very old dog and lives in Los Angeles, California.<br/></span>
